    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

  <span id="freeText2376600079566225566" style="display:none">Among the ashes of a dying world, an agent of the Commandant finds a letter. It reads: <i>Burn before reading.</i> Thus begins an unlikely correspondence between two rival agents hellbent on securing the best possible future for their warring factions. Now, what began as a taunt, a battlefield boast, grows into something more. Something epic. Something romantic. Something that could change the past and the future.<br /><br />Except the discovery of their bond would mean death for each of them. There's still a war going on, after all. And someone has to win that war.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_45839133').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_45839133').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_45839133').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {

<div id="review_2785759473" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2785759473" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2785759473?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-gay-yearning">trope-gay-yearning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-time-travel">trope-time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-sff">adult-sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2019-releases">2019-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-ff">lgbtq-ff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-rivals-to-lovers">trope-rivals-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2785759473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14635646929567721373"><blockquote>
  <em>“You asked me to tell truths. I have. What do I want? Understanding. Exchange. Victory. A game—hiding and discovery. You’re a swift opponent, Blue. You play long odds. You run the table. If we’re to be at war, we might as well entertain one another.”</em>
</blockquote><br/><br/><em>This Is How You Lose the Time War</em> is the kind of novel that dips in and out of minds, catches the sharp sun of memory and gleams, leaves its scent on its readers, like perfume transferred between lovers. As soon as you start to put more words in,</span>
  <span id="freeText14635646929567721373" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <em>“You asked me to tell truths. I have. What do I want? Understanding. Exchange. Victory. A game—hiding and discovery. You’re a swift opponent, Blue. You play long odds. You run the table. If we’re to be at war, we might as well entertain one another.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><em>This Is How You Lose the Time War</em> is the kind of novel that dips in and out of minds, catches the sharp sun of memory and gleams, leaves its scent on its readers, like perfume transferred between lovers. As soon as you start to put more words in, however, you stagger and come to bewilderment—like reaching for something and misjudging the distance, feeling your fingers close over nothing but air. I had to read this novel in small doses, swallowing its blows a little at a time and I reckon I’ll need several rereads to figure out all that I can’t say in words right now.<br /><br />Even now, I find it hard to describe the action of the novel, but—without spoiling anything—I can tell you that the first strand running through this loosely-braided narrative came in the form of a letter. The first of its kind was only pretend, an instant of self-indulgence, something like laying laughter over the dark, but it begun a circling of time for Red, the past cutting into the present like a whetted blade. The second letter was an abyss daring her to fall inside, and Red had a sense that she and Blue were all digging themselves deeper than ever before. By the third letter, Red felt that they were cutting their own throats by this: <strong>Two time traveling spies from rival factions divided between attack and diplomacy who, finding their way—<em>making</em> their way—through world after time-war-ravaged world, made contact and found love—and something that frightened them, too—across a void too profound to bridge with anything other than words.</strong><br /><br />The two women were more real to each other than reflections in a mirror and their scarred and hacked edges had borne witness to too many battles waged against time (and each other). They were like fish eyeing the hook, with too many forces ready to make siege weapons of their letters. In the sheer, shimmering improbability of the moment, however, they could almost pretend this love affair wasn’t a fool’s errand.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    And we’ll run again, the two of us, upthread and down, firefighter and fire starter, two predators only sated by each other’s words.
  </em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><em>This Is How You Lose the Time War</em> is not a light read by any stretch. It's a book of sustained beauty and lyricism that also works as a fractured mosaic of a novel—told in swift, brutal strokes, all wound into vertiginous loops of prose.<br /><br />It is difficult, at first, to get a firm grip on the slippery setting of <em>This Is How You Lose the Time War</em>. I felt like someone hurled unwary into a tale they didn’t understand, with people all around waiting for them to take up a part they didn’t know. There was a dream-like quality to the experience, as if those moments were divorced from the waking world by the strangeness of it all. But even with confusion painted on my face, the story made sense to me in a wordless way that could only be described as magic. Every word was worth savoring, and my own breath seemed to pipe in harmony.<br /><br />Which is why I think the novel would be irreducible by any easy categorization: <em>This Is How You Lose the Time War</em> is a time travel adventure, a sci-fi romp, poetry masquerading as prose, and a love story. It’s an intricate dance, and one that the authors render with agility, grace and ease. That they could pull it off at all—let alone so winningly—is something of a marvel itself, and I was left genuinely impressed.<br /><br />While <em>This Is How You Lose the Time War</em> is not written in verse, poetry lives in its pages. The authors are in thrilling command of their narrative gifts, and their language soars as they write of desire, longing, survival, and freedom.<br /><br />That said, those gifts can double as obstacles. As dizzying and immersive as the setting and premise are, <em>This Is How You Lose the Time War</em> is novel that is both exhilarating and exhausting—sometimes simultaneously. Even as I snatched hungrily at the next page, there were moments when the lyricism felt labored—the sentences so bedecked with metaphors and analogies that reading becomes akin to treading water in sodden clothes, barely keeping your nose and mouth above the surface—and I found myself sometimes craving a little restraint. Inside the long economy of a novel, too much prose—no matter how exquisite—can occasionally hamper the otherwise compelling flow, and, I think readers who can’t muster tame patience for tackling a few extra pages of mellifluous language might not find as much resonance.<br /><br />I’m confident, however, that those able to relax into the chaos will be as richly rewarded as I was when the strands eventually beautifully entwine together.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    Dearest, deepest Blue—
  </em>
  <br />
  <em>
    At the end as at the start, and through all the in-betweens, I love you. 
  </em>
  <br />
  <em>
    Red
  </em>
</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14635646929567721373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3394529525" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3394529525" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598112512p2/57797254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3394529525?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3394529525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5521390974545784890">This is the most fun I’ve had reading this writing style in a while! It’s such a creative, abstract, lyrical, and well-written love story that not only did I re-listen to each chapter twice on audiobook, but I also ended up borrowing the ebook just so that I could digest the writing via my eyeballs. There were many sensory experiences and beautifully crafted letters. The cat-and-mouse game between the two female protagonists is fun to read and the intimacy that builds up between them just by the</span>
  <span id="freeText5521390974545784890" style="display:none">This is the most fun I’ve had reading this writing style in a while! It’s such a creative, abstract, lyrical, and well-written love story that not only did I re-listen to each chapter twice on audiobook, but I also ended up borrowing the ebook just so that I could digest the writing via my eyeballs. There were many sensory experiences and beautifully crafted letters. The cat-and-mouse game between the two female protagonists is fun to read and the intimacy that builds up between them just by the letters alone is a great ride. It is not a perfect book and sometimes it can feel repetitive or filler-like due to the repeated format, but I am more so impressed by the creativity of layering all these different time periods and how the writers clearly had fun putting this together, including the twist at the end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5521390974545784890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2428553788" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2428553788" />
    <a title="Philip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30863291-philip"><img alt="Philip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527983001p2/30863291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2428553788?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Philip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Philip" href="/user/show/30863291-philip">Philip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/45839133-this-is-how-you-lose-the-time-war">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=2019-releases">2019-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=author-woman">author-woman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=hugo-2020">hugo-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=author-of-color">author-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=author-man">author-man</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=hugo">hugo</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2428553788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7555065362147711920">2ish stars.<br/><br/>What it comes down to is that I'm simply not enough of a romantic to enjoy this book. The appeal lies squarely in the flowery language written in love poems between two post-human women on opposite sides of a time travel war. I just happen to find love poetry more pretentious and mawkish than amorous or emotive. (Can it even really be considered romantic when one character addresses the other as "Dearest Blue-da-ba-dee?")<br/><br/>The rest of the book (characters, setting, plot) is left intenti</span>
  <span id="freeText7555065362147711920" style="display:none">2ish stars.<br /><br />What it comes down to is that I'm simply not enough of a romantic to enjoy this book. The appeal lies squarely in the flowery language written in love poems between two post-human women on opposite sides of a time travel war. I just happen to find love poetry more pretentious and mawkish than amorous or emotive. (Can it even really be considered romantic when one character addresses the other as "Dearest Blue-da-ba-dee?")<br /><br />The rest of the book (characters, setting, plot) is left intentionally indistinct and much of it is epistolary in format, so I was left feeling detached and dispassionate. Not enough is described about the characters to identify with them or care much about them outside the context of their forbidden romance. Not enough of the world is described to care much about what's going on with the war itself. As the authors write, “Some things are more important than winning.” When you don't care much about who wins or loses anyway, the point becomes moot.<br /><br /><a href="https://mrphilipslibrary.wordpress.com/2019/10/15/this-is-how-you-lose-the-time-war-by-amal-el-mohtar-and-max-gladstone/" rel="nofollow noopener">Posted in Mr. Philip's Library</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7555065362147711920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3445873420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13637546569921487935">I do not know how to write five star reviews.<br/><br/>Give me a book I hate and I’ll write a full-on thesis on it. Prime example: Just yesterday I spent <i>one human hour</i> on <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3602428355?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>a seven-page one star rant review</a>. And honestly? Time well spent.<br/><br/>But when it comes to something I truly love? I’m illiterate. Can’t read. Can’t write. Call me Jared, 19. What am I doing on this book site? Couldn’t tell you.<br/><br/>I WANT to scream about this from the rooftops. I want each and every one of you to read it, because it is utterly o</span>
  <span id="freeText13637546569921487935" style="display:none">I do not know how to write five star reviews.<br /><br />Give me a book I hate and I’ll write a full-on thesis on it. Prime example: Just yesterday I spent <i>one human hour</i> on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3602428355?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">a seven-page one star rant review</a>. And honestly? Time well spent.<br /><br />But when it comes to something I truly love? I’m illiterate. Can’t read. Can’t write. Call me Jared, 19. What am I doing on this book site? Couldn’t tell you.<br /><br />I WANT to scream about this from the rooftops. I want each and every one of you to read it, because it is utterly one of a kind and it’s gripping from page one and the characters are fantastic and the writing is witty and beautiful and it is…<br /><br />I tried to trick myself into stating all the ways in which it is amazing, but as always I got overwhelmed and ran out of words to describe it. (The one scenario in known human existence that can get me to shut up for even one second.)<br /><br />Anytime I write a five star review, I struggle to render perfection onto the page, and I just make myself want to reread.<br /><br />Damn...I really, really want to reread.<br /><br />Bottom line: Don’t take my insufficient words for it!!! But read this book immediately.<br /><br />---------------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />who the hell told this book it was allowed to end?<br /><br />review to come / 5 stars<br /><br />---------------<br /><i>currently-reading updates</i><br /><br />how far into this book were you when you realized it was unlike anything you'd ever read or would read, and also you were in love with it?<br /><br />for me it was page 14.<br /><br />---------------<br /><i>tbr review</i><br /><br />i'm a simple girl. i hear sapphic time travel, i add to my tbr</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2847935988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8545698454603893932"><b>Congratulations</b> to the 2020 Hugo winner for best novella! <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>But when I think of you, I want to be alone together. I want to strive against and for. I want to live in contact. I want to be a context for you, and you for me.<br/><br/>I love you, and I love you, and I want to find out what that means together.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><i>This Is How You Lose the Time War</i> is about two women, Red and Blue, on opposite sides of a time war, as they fall in love with each other via love letters. It… was a lot to process. This is mo</span>
  <span id="freeText8545698454603893932" style="display:none"><b>Congratulations</b> to the 2020 Hugo winner for best novella! <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>But when I think of you, I want to be alone together. I want to strive against and for. I want to live in contact. I want to be a context for you, and you for me.<br /><br />I love you, and I love you, and I want to find out what that means together.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><i>This Is How You Lose the Time War</i> is about two women, Red and Blue, on opposite sides of a time war, as they fall in love with each other via love letters. It… was a lot to process. This is more poetry than book, and I think maybe in another timeline, another time in my life, that would have annoyed me. In this case, I adored it. <br /><br />This is a novel about time that does not try to ground itself or stick to a place and a setting. Gladstone and El-Mohtar stick to flurid details of this world: Red’s technology-centric future, and Blue’s natural paradise. The chaotic details surround the reader from the start: the rise and fall of multiple Atlantises, the sheer amount of the timestream, and—the biggest threat—the sheer unwinnability of the war. Rather, it sticks to a love story, to the simpleness of caring. <br /><br />What does it actually mean to hunger as a crafted, manufactured creature? What does it mean to love as such? What does it mean when to desire is painful, and has consequences for both you and the other person? <br /><br />The letters are the standout, the flying colors of the novel. There is something very profound about this Romeo-Juliet esque love story, one neither of them have a chance at surviving from the start. Communicating is an act of bravery and it is through these acts of bravery that they fall in love. I went trawling through Wikipedia and found out this about the letters:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>..."Red's letters were written entirely by Gladstone, and Blue's by El-Mohtar; although they wrote a general outline beforehand, "the reactions of each character were developed with a genuine element of surprise on receiving each letter, and the scenes accompanying [the letters] were written using that emotional response"."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Don’t let all the doom fool you, though; this is by no means a sad book. The story of Red and Blue falling in love through time is one that I spent more time smiling at than crying at. I loved getting to know these characters. I hungered to know them more. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I want to meet you in every place I have loved.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />If you like: <br />🌿Time travel, or time travel wars<br />🌿Tender sapphic romance<br />🌿Thinking about the innate pain and humiliation of desire<br />🌿Very very gorgeous writing<br />🌿Crying. i wish i were kidding i cried so much it was kind of bad<br />...then I think you will like this book.<br /><br /><a href="https://ellexamines.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/ellexamines" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/ellexamines" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/ellexamines/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://sptfy.com/4F6I" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="https://ellexamines.carrd.co/" rel="nofollow noopener">About</a> |</span>
  <a data-text-id="8545698454603893932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2019-shelf">2019-shelf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2815454801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3097652767089039009">Re-Read 12/17/19:<br/><br/>I've been thinking about this novella for months since I read it last. It just kept sticking to the roof of my mouth and I loved the flavor sooo much. :)<br/><br/>It's poetry. A tragic romance written as a super-hard-SF spy vs spy. And it's poetry. :)<br/><br/>I LOVE this so much. <br/><br/><br/><br/>Original review:<br/><br/>Damn excellent SF novella. I won't have any problems nominating this for next year's Hugo. It's poetical, yo. Not only poetical, but delightfully unforced in its romance... even as the time war rages betwe</span>
  <span id="freeText3097652767089039009" style="display:none">Re-Read 12/17/19:<br /><br />I've been thinking about this novella for months since I read it last. It just kept sticking to the roof of my mouth and I loved the flavor sooo much. :)<br /><br />It's poetry. A tragic romance written as a super-hard-SF spy vs spy. And it's poetry. :)<br /><br />I LOVE this so much. <br /><br /><br /><br />Original review:<br /><br />Damn excellent SF novella. I won't have any problems nominating this for next year's Hugo. It's poetical, yo. Not only poetical, but delightfully unforced in its romance... even as the time war rages between heavy tech and heavy biopunk up and down multiple timelines in a game of Go! that stretches to near-infinity.<br /><br />Wait. Did I say romance? Yep. Hard SF romance, so light and deft in its hardcore science it becomes a whirlwind of ambiance designed only to paint glorious pictures and denude us in playful taste, hunger, and excitement.<br /><br />The novella is mostly written in epistolary format, which I love, and it evokes so much crazy longing between these two enemies that it is pretty obvious that they have completely fallen for each other by the third exchange. :) Even if they're plotting their opposite's death by strange and subtle threads and means up and down the timelines. :)<br /><br />Gloriously so, the tastes of history are obscure and rich. The format of the letters, even more so. Written in plants, seeds, only readable through taste or stings. Scorched space battlements and desolate beaches, dinosaurs and playful birds. Did I say this was poetry? Poetry as prose? The hunger is palpable, the romance, desperate. <br /><br />Sure, they're post-human women, but the shape doesn't matter when they take whatever shapes they like. The feeling is everything. <br /><br />So how does it turn out? Is it a tragedy? I will not say. But I feel lighter than air after reading this. It deserves a careful read. An engrossing read. A consuming read. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3097652767089039009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2577285305353169054">This is a book so beautifully written and perfectly conceived that I know any words I write about it will pale in comparison. I want this entire book tattooed over every inch of my body so that I can remember every single word forever.</span>

    <a title="Emily " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2377230-emily"><img alt="Emily " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486778976p2/2377230.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily " href="/user/show/2377230-emily">Emily </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2377230-emily?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2377230-emily?shelf=short-story">short-story</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2930816596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17547947658357436607">Almost all my Goodread friends are raving about this. I just didn't like it. I never really understood why the characters fell in love, there's no explanation about what is really going on with the two sides and the writing style was just too... "extra" for me. It's very literary and poetic, it's all words and not much substance. It just wasn't for me.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3541902558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3541902558" />
    <a title="s.penkevich" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6431467-s-penkevich"><img alt="s.penkevich" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587089836p2/6431467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3541902558?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="s.penkevich" class="user" itemprop="url" name="s.penkevich" href="/user/show/6431467-s-penkevich">s.penkevich</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431467-s-penkevich?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431467-s-penkevich?shelf=time_travel">time_travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431467-s-penkevich?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431467-s-penkevich?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431467-s-penkevich?shelf=epistolary">epistolary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3541902558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9991474503386392518">‘<i>I want to be a context for you, and you for me.</i>’<br/><br/>There is something uniquely affecting when love is painted against the backdrop of the limitlessness of space and time. The effect has been done many times over but nothing can prepare you for the extraordinary beauty in which <i>This is How You Lose the Time War</i> allows you to experience love stretching out and weaving across time and dimensions to examine just how infinite it can possibly be. A spark of emotion that shines through galaxies reduced t</span>
  <span id="freeText9991474503386392518" style="display:none">‘<i>I want to be a context for you, and you for me.</i>’<br /><br />There is something uniquely affecting when love is painted against the backdrop of the limitlessness of space and time. The effect has been done many times over but nothing can prepare you for the extraordinary beauty in which <i>This is How You Lose the Time War</i> allows you to experience love stretching out and weaving across time and dimensions to examine just how infinite it can possibly be. A spark of emotion that shines through galaxies reduced to dust, the countless rises and falls of mortal empires, the lifespans of all human feats and follies. Co-written by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4175512.Amal_El_Mohtar" title="Amal El-Mohtar" rel="nofollow noopener">Amal El-Mohtar</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3405346.Max_Gladstone" title="Max Gladstone" rel="nofollow noopener">Max Gladstone</a>, each writing one of the two protagonists, the novel is a soaring epistalatory sapphic romance between two rival time-traveling agents in a war between their respective societies to control and rewrite the multiverse in order to eradicate the other. Spawn by a private battlefield provocation, the two agents become caught in a maelstrom of self-discovery and romance corresponding by letters as they chase each other across time and space in a playful and imaginative novel so searingly beautiful the cosmos can barely contain it.<br /><br />These two authors have created something charmingly original in Time War, enhanced by the distinct dueling voices of the authors as their prose communicates and responds to each other along with their characters. Many of these letters, particularly in the novel’s latter half, blossom into pure ethereal poetry. On occasion it dips into purple prose, as one letter admits, however, what a clever sentiment for a profession of love between characters named Red and Blue to evolve into purple. The writing remains crisp, rotating between short narration and the correspondence between the two, allowing the narrative to progress as strongly on wings of emotion as it does the chain of events. What transpires is often intentionally vague as no time is wasted on much exposition or explanation, but fully immerses you in a world you won’t quite grasp or understand. It’s as if this gorgeous landscape of the multiverse were simply a blur as you are focused on the interaction between Red and Blue, much the way the world around you fades from focus in the first moments of love.<br /><br />Ultimately, any attempt at concreteness in a universe in a constant state of flux and revision would be beside the point, and the vagueness reflects that. It is only though the shared connection between Red and Blue that we can find a stable focal point as they pass through a kaleidoscope of time. Much like the way the pair gives context to one another, our only context is through them as well. They are each other’s only tether to stability in an unstable reality.<br /><br />‘<i>When did it happen? Or has it always happened? Like your victory, love spreads back through time.</i>’<br /><br />Entire multi-dimensions are shifted, burned or woven together on the battlefield of time between Garden, an organic and collectivist society from which Blue has grown, and Agency, a post-singularity mechanical society that created Red. They are locked in an eternal time-war of which the specifics and origins of are rarely addressed and even then are quite vague. The novel makes reference to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18135.Romeo_and_Juliet" title="Romeo and Juliet by William Shakespeare" rel="nofollow noopener">Romeo and Juliet</a> in narrative and thematically (the play, it is said, has different endings in each strand of time), and shares it’s notion of a long-standing feud where all existing players have forgotten why but continue to play it out to the point of extreme violence. What they are doing exactly is a bit elusive but strands are altered by, say, helping a city build a port or ensuring a mathematical formula survives the destruction of Atlantis: little things that add up over centuries to create wholly different versions of reality that are fought over.<br /><blockquote>‘<i>In the war they wage through time, what lasting advantage comes from murdering ghosts, who, with a slight shift of threads, will return to life or live different lives that never bright them to the executioner’s blade?...No death sticks but the one that matters.</i>’ </blockquote><br />‘<i>What a microcosm we are of the war as a whole, you and I,</i>’ Blue writes to Red early on, ‘<i>An action and an equal and opposite reaction.</i>’ The two women--they identify as she/her and can take on human form though you’d be hard pressed to form a definite image of what they look like based on the various hints--who’s designation as Red and Blue help to impress an idea as mere players in a game, are equals of one another, rivals ever, which is the initial attraction between the them. ‘<i>They were separate, they did not speak, but each shaped the other, even as they were shaped in turn.</i>’ What begins as a game of hunter and hunted in boasting and taunting letters quickly gives way to deep conversations about the self that makes them aware they have an agency beyond their respective Agencies and despite being weapons of war have a taste for the finer and beautiful things in life. In those moments they realize there is a hole inside them that only the other can fill. And as their love grows, they begin to wonder--partly due to the millenia of time they criss-cross during their budding attraction--if perhaps the love didn’t just arrive but had always been there. As with any sci-fi involving time travel, there is the inevitable paradox of events and free-will within a shifting reality and the two authors harness this paradox into their novel towards an exquisite and emotional end.<br /><br />‘<i>There’s a kind of time travel in letters, isn’t there?</i>’<br /><br />‘<i>Letters are structures, not events,</i>’ Red writes to Blue, ‘<i>Yours give me a place to live inside.</i>’ This beautiful refuge from war they’ve found in their secret correspondence also becomes a commentary on language and communication itself. In whimsical sci-fi nature, they write in abstract languages found in reading the structure of leaves on a plant or decoding rings on a tree (just let it happen, it’s super cool), which reflects the way the tools of writing shape how we write--a topic often written upon by philosopher <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4132.Jacques_Derrida" title="Jacques Derrida" rel="nofollow noopener">Jacques Derrida</a>. Their secret letters envelope the secrecy of their relationship and dangers they face even reading letters from the enemy, which is fascinating to think of considering a digital age where communication can occur through images (entire conversations can be had with emojis and memes) or other non-alphabetic communication. <br /><br />In our modern world we continue to embrace non-verbal communication that relationships can be built from, such as how with online dating many people exist only in messages to one another before meeting and form an attraction that way. It is a beautiful notion to consider how through just our words we can fall in love with the essence of another by showing an understanding, empathy and passion for the thoughts of each other (when I first met my partner we met in person only three times before she moved back to Ireland so for months we got to know each other through long late night texting and her sending me letters, so love across distance has always spoken to me pretty well). Messages written at one place in time, sent, and received in another transmitting emotions across time and space. ‘<i>Books are letters in bottles,</i>’ one letter reads, ‘<i>cast into the waves of time, from one person trying to save the world to another.</i>’ All books are love letters, if you think about it. One person sending out a message in hopes someone will understand and understand them in turn, an abstract connection that reaches even beyond the grave. There is a voyeuristic sense to this novel--reading their letters and all--but it reminds us of our primal instincts that desire connection and the fireworks of emotion that come from first contact with it. It is nearly impossible to not be swept up in their romance and feel their fears, pains, and needs standing naked and unafraid before one another, like a tree in winter unashamed of it’s gnarled limbs. <br /><br />‘<i>Love is what we have, against time and death, against all the powers ranged to crush us down.</i>’<br /><br />There is a subtle shadow of dread cast across their saga keeping the reader keenly aware that their taboo relationship is always threatened by the larger world in which they exist. Agency traces Blue’s exploits and wishes to set a trap for her, one Red will be used to ensure the success of the mission. Betrayal exists in the peripheries of this novel at all times, especially when they begin to open up hoping this isn’t just some long con. Poison is an important theme throughout the novel, with the women taunting each other that any letter could be laced with it and choosing to read forward anyways. It reminds us of how we remove our armor and open ourselves up to pain when we choose to love. War begets death and suffering, and the two players have entered into this affair knowing the risks but plunging on ahead regardless. <br /><br />‘<i>I want to meet you in every place I have loved.</i>’<br /><br />It is difficult to say much more without spoiling anything in this clever plotted novel. It is one that encourages an immediate reread, as clues and puzzle pieces are weaved into the novel much like the way our heroines weave space and time together for their purposes. It is an extraordinary little book that somehow manages to never feel like a gimmick despite it’s inventive and quirky nature. Time, place, love, and war all become a potent concoction for one of the most tender and vulnerable romances I’ve ever read. I could praise it all day long but, as is written in one of the cosmic letters, ‘<i>I am the songbird running out of air, and I must breathe.</i>’<br /><br /><b>4.5/5</b><br /><br />‘<i>I want to be a body for you. I want to chase you, find you, I want to be eluded and teased and adored; I want to be defeated and victorious—I want you to cut me, sharpen me. I want to drink tea beside you in ten years or a thousand. Flowers grow far away on a planet they’ll call Cephalus, and these flowers bloom once a century, when the living star and its black-hole binary enter conjunction.I want to fix you a bouquet of them, gathered across eight hundred thousand years, so you can draw our whole engagement in a single breath, all the ages we’ve shaped together.</i>’</span>
  <a data-text-id="9991474503386392518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3148271603" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3148271603" />
    <a title="Cecily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1199525-cecily"><img alt="Cecily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480285828p2/1199525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3148271603?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cecily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cecily" href="/user/show/1199525-cecily">Cecily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=scifi-future-speculative-fict">scifi-future-speculative-fict</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=epistolary-and-letters">epistolary-and-letters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=love-not-soppy-romance">love-not-soppy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=sexuality-gender-lgbtq">sexuality-gender-lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=landscape-location-protagonist">landscape-location-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=detective-mystery-crime">detective-mystery-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3148271603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12197667612807980414">"<i>All good stories travel from the outside.</i>"<br/><br/>This is a passionate, genre-storming prose poem about temptation and the paradox of opposites that are not: of hunter and prey, tempter and victim - one and the same. <br/><br/>“<i>I want to chase you, find you, I want to be eluded and teased and adored; I want to be defeated and victorious - I want you to cut me, sharpen me.</i>”<br/> <br/><b>Irresistible</b><br/><br/>The first temptation is to defy the instruction to "Burn before reading", and the climax hinges on whether or not to succumb to t</span>
  <span id="freeText12197667612807980414" style="display:none">"<i>All good stories travel from the outside.</i>"<br><br>This is a passionate, genre-storming prose poem about temptation and the paradox of opposites that are not: of hunter and prey, tempter and victim - one and the same. <br><br>“<i>I want to chase you, find you, I want to be eluded and teased and adored; I want to be defeated and victorious - I want you to cut me, sharpen me.</i>”<br> <br><b>Irresistible</b><br><br>The first temptation is to defy the instruction to "Burn before reading", and the climax hinges on whether or not to succumb to the urge to read a poison pen letter. In between, there are the temptations of rule-breaking (including the rules of genre), devising and rising to reckless challenges, and the lure of forbidden love. No serpent or apple, but there is the possibility of an Eden.<br><br><b>Battling through time</b><br><br>Red (written by Max Gladstone) and Blue (written by Amal El-Mohtar) work for opposing organisations: the post-human cyborg Agency and biopunk Garden, respectively: “flash and dash” versus “patient planting and pruning”. Their bodies, personalities, and words reflect that… to begin with. <br><br>“<i>What a microcosm we are of the war as a whole, you and I. The physics of us. An action and an equal and opposite reaction. My viney-hivey elfworld, as you say, versus your techy-mechy dystopia.</i>”<br><br>They travel time in unexplained ways to shape and guard the future their bosses desire, trying to outwit Orwell’s famous line in <b>1984</b> (see my review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23327919" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>): “<i>Who controls the past controls the future: who controls the present controls the past.</i>”<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580163776i/28853805._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>The authors</i> (<a href="https://amalelmohtar.com/2017/11/05/this-is-how-you-lose-the-time-war/" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a>.)<br><br><b>Epistolary love</b><br><br>“<i>There’s a kind of time travel in letters</i>”. <br>They are letters in the loosest sense: steganography in tree rings, seeds, molten lava, bee stings, stars and more. Almost out of sight, the shadow Seeker gathers, works, and consumes the broken, illegible remnants.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566211836i/28014387._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>Message in lava?</i> (<a href="https://www.nationalgeographic.org/encyclopedia/magma/" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a>.)<br><br>"<i>Assassinations become assignations.</i>" <br>It’s a sort of Romeo and Juliet up and down the twisty threads of time: braiding, cutting, cauterising. A shimmering kaleidoscope of butterfly effects. <br><br>“<i>I have known you since before I knew you.</i>”<br>Literally true for those who travel in time. Who loved who first? Who existed first? <br>“<i>Under the spreading chestnut tree, I made you and you made me.</i>”<br><br><b>What sort of novel is this?</b><br><br>It’s <s>un</s><b>poly</b>categorisable, and revels in that. Genres include: sci-fi (minus the science), time-travel, alternative history, speculative, futuristic, dystopian, Utopian, poetry, epistolary, action thriller, espionage, new weird, LGBTQ+ love, fantasy, magical realism, tragedy, comedy… <br><br><b>Freedom from futility</b><br><br>“<i>What lasting advantage comes from murdering ghosts, who, with a slight shift of threads will return to life or live different lives that never bring them to the executioner’s blade?</i>”<br><br>It’s red and blue, not black and white. Their love is transgressive not because they are both female, but because they are meant to be enemies, even though there is no binary sense of good and evil. When you’re constantly rewriting events, right and wrong become as mercurial as “history” itself. <br><br>“<i>Wars are dense with causes and effects.</i>” Time wars especially, and when any battle can be rerun with a different outcome, war is even more futile than in a linear, single universe. That realisation is liberating.<br><br><b>Subtle diversity</b><br><br>Red, Blue, and Red’s Commandant are brave, intelligent, strong, women, taking charge of their lives. I appreciate normalising that by not shouting about it, but I don’t think I’d have noticed their gender if it hadn’t been stated, which rather dilutes the point. However, I prefer subtlety to sledgehammers: immediately after this, I read <b>The Psychology of Time Travel</b> (see my review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2713223143" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>), which constantly reminds readers how diverse the characters are. <br><br><b>Up, down, back, forward, but how?</b><br><br>Details of the mechanics would be out of place in such ethereal writing, but sometimes it’s frustratingly opaque:<br>“<i>In downthread server farms couched in remnant icebergs’ hearts, she circles back upon her tail.</i>”<br>I wanted just a little more understanding, especially early on. <br><br>I found the idea of <b>up</b>thread being the “stable past” and <b>down</b>thread being the “fraying future” so counter-intuitive, I had to keep checking my notes. Obviously the pages have a gravitational pull from top to bottom (“<i>How strange to uncover things in sequence</i>”, Red says of books), but I visualise the threads of the past hanging below the present. My fault, but distracting.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580163776i/28853806._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>Braided sweet grass</i> (<a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Braided_Sweet_Grass.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a>.)<br><br><b>Quotes</b><br><br>•	“Most strands lack Atlantis altogether, knowing the place only through dreams and mad poets’ madder whispers.”<br><br>•	“I want to be a context for you, and you for me.”<br><br>•	“Threads of time sing with the light, swift footfalls of… soldiers.”<br><br>•	“Moss breathes fumes of sleep.”<br><br>•	“Pollen thickens the air with wisdom.”<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580163876i/28853811._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>Fan art, by Kori Michele</i> (<a href="https://twitter.com/korimichele/status/1155966519588712453" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a>.)<br><br>I’ve <b>added line breaks</b> to these, but not changed the words.<br><br>“London… one strand over - <br>is the kind of London other Londons dream: <br>sepia tinted, skies strung with dirigibles. <br>The viciousness of empire acknowledged <br>only as a rosy backdrop glow redolent of spice and petalled sugar. <br>Mannered as a novel, <br>filthy only where story requires it, <br>all meat pies and monarchy.”<br><br>“The dreams towards which she rocks him… <br>will spiral tendrils of possibility from this strand into others, <br>send tremors to shift and shake the future’s boughs in Garden’s direction.”<br><br>“As the great <i>Gallumfry</i> lists planetward, <br>raining escape pods, <br>as battle stations wilt like flowers tossed into film, <br>as radio bands crackle triumph <br>and swiftskimmers swoop after fleeing voidtails, <br>as guns speak their last arguments into mute space, <br>she slips away.”<br><br>“I wick the longing into thread, <br>pass it through your needle eye, <br>and sew it into hiding somewhere beneath my skin, <br>embroider my next letter to you one stitch at a time.”<br><br>“Space here is sick. <br>Thick. <br>Slick. <br>She drowns in cloying honey-heavy light. <br>Her passage through vacuum feels like sliding over meat… <br>Far away and too, too near shines a sun that is an eye with a great hourglass pupil like a goat’s, <br>sweeping space for weaknesses to improve, exploit… <br>Thick fluid space opens.”<br><br><b>Dedicated, recommended, tempted</b> - or not<br><br>This is dedicated “<i>To you. PS. Yes, you.</i>” Perhaps Blue’s recommendation of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/827276.Travel_Light" title="Travel Light by Naomi Mitchison" rel="nofollow noopener">Travel Light</a> is to me as well as Red. GR says it’s a fantasy with a strong female lead, written by a Scottish Victorian. Back to temptation.<br><br>The TV rights have been optioned, with the original writers doing the scripts. I don’t want to see concrete manifestation of characters and worlds that are so ethereal, but curiosity may win.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12197667612807980414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3131015543" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3131015543" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3131015543?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781508287056" href="/book/show/42996336-this-is-how-you-lose-the-time-war">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=book-a-book-club">book-a-book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3131015543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6483319651604712178">Wow! Whether you end up enjoying this book or not, I think you will have to admit it is a very unique and poetic approach to such a dark and gritty sci-fi war drama. In fact, I am not sure that everyone that finds themselves usually enjoying sci-fi will enjoy this one because it is not what you would normally expect.<br/><br/>I really liked this book overall. I cannot say that in the end I understood everything that happened, but I think that is okay in this case. The poetry, the character development, an</span>
  <span id="freeText6483319651604712178" style="display:none">Wow! Whether you end up enjoying this book or not, I think you will have to admit it is a very unique and poetic approach to such a dark and gritty sci-fi war drama. In fact, I am not sure that everyone that finds themselves usually enjoying sci-fi will enjoy this one because it is not what you would normally expect.<br /><br />I really liked this book overall. I cannot say that in the end I understood everything that happened, but I think that is okay in this case. The poetry, the character development, and the relationships were more important than the world building. However, I think there are some who will appreciate the sci-fi world building that serves as the stage for the main storyline.<br /><br />Some may note that this novella is categorized as a "Romance". When I hear the word "Romance" I think of bodice rippers with shirtless men in kilts and damsels in tattered blouses lusting after them. That is NOT the "Romance" you will find here. No sex or gratuitous exchange of bodily fluids. Just strong longing, passion, and desire through words. <br /><br />If you like unique sci-fi, you might like this. If you like heart-wrenching love stories, you might like this. If you like both of those things, you will love this! Give it a try!<br /><br />NOTE: I forgot to add this when I originally wrote my review but meant to add it. I do think that many might find this hard to get into at first. I listened to it and ended up listening to a good portion of the beginning twice. I am not saying that it will definitely click through after you struggle through the beginning, but don't be surprised by a tough start.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6483319651604712178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3182427404" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3182427404" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3182427404?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=hugo-nebula">hugo-nebula</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=locus-winner">locus-winner</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3182427404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5444830600918506876">A divide - organic or artificial, no matter - sometimes seems made for reaching out across, for sifting through the abyss of difference to find the threads that braid us together.<br/><br/>This is a story we crave - of bridging the gap, of mending the rift, of star-crossed lovers surmounting the insurmountable.<blockquote>
  <i>“She climbs upthread and down; she braids and unbraids history’s hair.<br/>Red rarely sleeps, but when she does, she lies still, eyes closed in the dark, and lets herself see lapis, taste iris petals </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5444830600918506876" style="display:none">A divide - organic or artificial, no matter - sometimes seems made for reaching out across, for sifting through the abyss of difference to find the threads that braid us together.<br><br>This is a story we crave - of bridging the gap, of mending the rift, of star-crossed lovers surmounting the insurmountable.<blockquote>
  <i>“She climbs upthread and down; she braids and unbraids history’s hair.<br>Red rarely sleeps, but when she does, she lies still, eyes closed in the dark, and lets herself see lapis, taste iris petals and ice, hear a blue jay’s shriek. She collects blues and keeps them.<br>When she is sure no one is watching, she rereads the letters she’s carved into herself.”</i>
</blockquote>Let’s try to make it sound simpler and linear. There are two sides in the neverending time war, waged upthread and downthread the countless braids of time by two opposing sides: the <i> “viny-hivey elfworlds”</i> of the Garden and <i> “techy-mechy dystopia”</i> of the Agency, so different in form but so similar in the oppressive singlemindedness. Blue and Red are the opposing agents, post-human, really, who secretly start what quickly becomes an <b>epistolary romance building up to the scream of soul, written in letters and flowers and tea leaves and birds and rope knots and lava flows</b>, a meeting of intertwined minds and souls, a longing for the other who is both different and yet the same. <blockquote>
<i>“It's amazing how much blue there is in the world if you look. You're different colors of flame. Bismuth burns blue, and cerium, germanium, and arsenic. See? I pour you into things.”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1588531010i/29407049._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote>Surreal, febrile, lush - these are the words that spring to mind when I look for descriptors. To work as intended, it needs to have<b> a dreamlike quality</b>, and on that front it delivers determinedly and doggedly. <blockquote>
  <i>“So in this letter I am yours. Not Garden’s, not your mission’s, but yours, alone.<br>I am yours in other ways as well: yours as I watch the world for your signs, apophenic as a haruspex; yours as I debate methods, motives, chances of delivery; yours as I review your words by their sequence, their sound, smell, taste, taking care no one memory of them becomes too worn. Yours. Still, I suspect you will appreciate the token.”<i></i></i>
</blockquote>And the prose, oh the prose… It’s almost mockingly self-aware -<b> when you mix Red and Blue, you get purple</b>. Oh yes you do. It states so outright, making sure you don’t miss it. It could have let it be more subtle, but then I would not have grinned in delight at this pun which my brain already had made a few times in this story of mixing Red and Blue:<br><br><b>
  <i>“I veer rhapsodic; my prose purples.”</i>
</b><br><br>This story hinges on the pull and embrace of purplish prose, of the ornate lush febrile narration, on the magic of elaborate weaving of words. It’s both alluring and suffocating, deliberately so. It’s synesthesthetic, almost tactile, the feel of a migrainous aura. I resist its pull and yet so readily succumb to it, just as intended.<blockquote>
<i>“You’ve whetted me like a stone. I feel almost invincible in our battles’ wake: a kind of Achilles, fleet footed and light of touch. Only in this nonexistent place our letters weave do I feel weak.<br>How I love to have no armor here.”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1588531529i/29407078._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote>This story reminds me of the fragments of those dreams you always seem to have just before waking, the dreams that you can’t quite fully recall but that are right there right at the brink of consciousness. <blockquote>
  <i>“I sought loneliness when I was young. You’ve seen me there: on my promontory, patient and unaware.<br>But when I think of you, I want to be alone together. I want to strive against and for. I want to live in contact. I want to be a context for you, and you for me.<br>I love you, and I love you, and I want to find out what that means together.”</i>
</blockquote>I see what it’s doing. I see what it’s working hard to make you feel. I see the puppeteer strings designed to play with your emotions.<br><br>I see that it’s not even trying to be subtle.<br><br><b>And yet I’m powerless to resist its allure.</b><blockquote>
  <i>“I don’t give a shit who wins this war, Garden or the Agency—towards whose Shift the arc of the universe bends.<br>But maybe this is how we win, Red.<br>You and me.<br>This is how we win.”</i>
</blockquote><br>———————————<br><br>For a similar feel (and flawless execution), read Catherynne M. Valente’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12887497.Silently_and_Very_Fast" title="Silently and Very Fast by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">Silently and Very Fast</a> (my review here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/309595463">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a>)<br><br>———————<br><br>My Hugo and Nebula Awards Reading Project 2020: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3295830569">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5444830600918506876" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2803609879" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2803609879" />
    <a title="Billie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3915342-billie"><img alt="Billie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421200946p2/3915342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2803609879?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Billie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Billie" href="/user/show/3915342-billie">Billie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/41093488-this-is-how-you-lose-the-time-war">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2803609879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3491972465587556903">Okay. So. Hmm. I loved the love story aspect of it and generally got the gist of what was going on, but there was some big-picture world building that either went completely over my head (likely) or was missing (possible). Being dumped into the middle of a story that has been going on, off the page, for who-knows-how-long can be disorienting. And maybe it was meant to be. Or maybe I'm just not smart enough for this book. Or maybe it was a mis-step on the part of the authors. Whatever the reason </span>
  <span id="freeText3491972465587556903" style="display:none">Okay. So. Hmm. I loved the love story aspect of it and generally got the gist of what was going on, but there was some big-picture world building that either went completely over my head (likely) or was missing (possible). Being dumped into the middle of a story that has been going on, off the page, for who-knows-how-long can be disorienting. And maybe it was meant to be. Or maybe I'm just not smart enough for this book. Or maybe it was a mis-step on the part of the authors. Whatever the reason for it, I finished the book feeling like I had missed something, like there was something there that I wasn't getting. Whatever it was, it made me feel stupid and, honestly, like the authors were having a laugh at my expense. I've no doubt that the book will be lauded for its cleverness and some well-meaning person will try to explain it all to me like I'm a four-year-old and I'll end up feeling even more lacking for having not gotten it. And I know that not every book is for every reader and I am obviously not the right readerly fit for this particular volume. But, if you're going to make me feel stupid, do it on a China Mieville level that makes me want to learn more and get smarter and not in a way that feels like I've just read a two hundred-page inside joke that only the "cool" kids will get.<br /><br />Gods. I apparently have feelings about this one and I didn't realize how deeply negative those feelings were until I started typing this. I still liked the love story, though. It felt rather Nick Bantock-ish, which was a nostalgic kind of fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3491972465587556903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer1457430305458982049">Despite struggling for the first 50 pages, I eventually got into the flow of this book and I absolutely fell in love. <br/>Every single sentence of every letter made me want to burst into tears. The writing of this was the most poetic, lyrical writing I have EVER read. <br/>Despite barely knowing blue and red (and only knowing them for 200 pages), they become people I can think of say “I know them”. <br/>To say this book is amazing is an understatement and I’m so glad I pushed through the beginning. </span>

<div id="review_3139331752" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3139331752" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3139331752?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2020">year-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3139331752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13259040762973380935"><b>Actual Rating: 1.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Well I’m incredibly sad that I didn’t enjoy this more given all the rave reviews & what sounded like a super intriguing premise.<br/><br/>Agents of two opposing factions, time traveling through what is described as “braids” of alternate realities & dimensions, falling in love against their better judgement. Also they’re queer. Literally no part of this premise sounds bad to me.<br/><br/>Unfortunately it’s the execution of this idea that sends this book into a nosedive for me.<br/><br/>Normally I don’t</span>
  <span id="freeText13259040762973380935" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 1.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Well I’m incredibly sad that I didn’t enjoy this more given all the rave reviews &amp; what sounded like a super intriguing premise.<br /><br />Agents of two opposing factions, time traveling through what is described as “braids” of alternate realities &amp; dimensions, falling in love against their better judgement. Also they’re queer. Literally no part of this premise sounds bad to me.<br /><br />Unfortunately it’s the execution of this idea that sends this book into a nosedive for me.<br /><br />Normally I don’t mind a bit of flowery writing. Some of my favorite authors are known for their superfluous &amp; whimsical styles.<br /><br /><b>But oh boy are we talking full on flower garden, here.</b><br /><br />This book so chalk full of complicated metaphors, awkward turns of phrase, and segmented scenery that I just couldn’t find a comfortable footing at all while I read.<br /><br />I understand that this was likely exactly the intent of the authors when they crafted this tale. It’s not necessarily about the situation, not about the individual scenarios our characters find themselves in. Rather, it’s about their relationship development. <br /><br />And I guess maybe that had me feeling sort of off balance? Like I could’ve done with more information about the time war that’s mentioned in the title, but that just isn’t really meant to be the focus of the story. <br /><br />There’s almost no feeling of concreteness to the anything that takes place, if that makes sense. Genuinely, there were times while reading this book that I really didn’t know what visual or emotional experience the author was trying to steer me toward, and it left me feeling adrift &amp; unconnected to the story. <br /><br />I found my inner reader saying “...well okay then” to herself quite a lot more than usual &amp; that just didn’t make for a comfortable reading experience. Like I was just wading slowly through a nonsensical, Alice in Wonderland adjacent world of words &amp; waiting for solid pieces to latch onto. <br /><br />But I will say that I did like the two main characters &amp; their “enemies to lovers but still enemies sorta” romance, and I found the resolution incredibly fitting for the story being told. It addresses a small problem I’d been having for 99% of my reading so I appreciated that. <br /><br />This isn’t something that would be near the top of my list of recommendations by any means, but if you’re a fan of a more abstract story about two badass women falling in love &amp; inter-dimensional time travel, maybe it’s for you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13259040762973380935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1241553985248870067" style="display:none">3.5 stars <br /><br />I actually finished this book 2 days ago but had no idea what I wanted to rate it. <br /><br />This book is a sapphic love story between two rival spies on different sides of a war fought through time. Chapters consist of short periods of time war plot with letter correspondence between the two happening between chapters. It’s beautifully written, particularly the letters and the ending. But I did find the ending to be a bit predictable and the overall plot, while interesting at times, wasn’t really the point because the book was so short. I think the characters and the plot of this book will fade for me very quickly and leave just a feeling of “that was a lovely, weird little book.” </span>

  <span id="freeText17814411246946552201" style="display:none">I kept on trying to figure out why this book did not land for me, and I think what I'm settling on is I would have preferred if this were told in letters only, kinda Sleeping Giants style.<br />I missed substance in the chapters, they felt like fluff to get to the letters. If this had been a full novel where you never know if there'll be a letter in the current or mission, I'd probably have enjoyed that too.<br />But... that's just not the point of this novella. And I think that's okay. I just wished this had been a 5 start for me, the way it seems to be for many, but I ended up at a similar point to you.</span>
