<div id="review_2996243982" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2996243982" />
    <a title="Blaine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2922102-blaine"><img alt="Blaine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505955717p2/2922102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2996243982?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blaine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blaine" href="/user/show/2922102-blaine">Blaine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2922102-blaine?shelf=from-library">from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2922102-blaine?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2922102-blaine?shelf=to-buy">to-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2922102-blaine?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2996243982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6458923021709231367"><blockquote>I want to meet you in every place I ever loved. Listen to me. I am your echo. I would rather break the world than lose you.<br/>...<br/>I want to chase you, find you, I want to be eluded and teased and adored; I want to be defeated and victorious—I want you to cut me, sharpen me. I want to drink tea beside you in ten years or a thousand. Flowers grow far away on a planet they’ll call Cephalus, and these flowers bloom once a century, when the living star and its black-hole binary enter conjunction. I want </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText6458923021709231367" style="display:none"><blockquote>I want to meet you in every place I ever loved. Listen to me. I am your echo. I would rather break the world than lose you.<br />...<br />I want to chase you, find you, I want to be eluded and teased and adored; I want to be defeated and victorious—I want you to cut me, sharpen me. I want to drink tea beside you in ten years or a thousand. Flowers grow far away on a planet they’ll call Cephalus, and these flowers bloom once a century, when the living star and its black-hole binary enter conjunction. I want to fix you a bouquet of them, gathered across eight hundred thousand years, so you can draw our whole engagement in a single breath, all the ages we’ve shaped together.</blockquote><br />The only things I knew about <i>This is How You Lose the Time War</i> before reading it were: 1) it was told through a series of letters between two agents traveling through time while fighting on opposite sides of a war, and 2) it has a cool-looking cover. I’d recommend reading it with that same limited knowledge.<br /><br />But perhaps you need more convincing. Red is a part of the Agency, traveling through strands of time and parallel worlds trying to give her side an edge in their war against the Garden. She is mechanical, technological. Blue is part of the Garden, traveling through those same strands and worlds trying to give her side an edge in their war against the Agency. She was literally grown from a seed. Red and Blue leave messages for each other after foiling each other’s plans. A few are paper letters; most are messages creatively hidden in items like the rings of a tree, seeds, an owl pellet, a lava flow. At first, the messages are gleeful and taunting. As time passes, and the agents get to know each other, well ... that’s where the drama unfolds.<br /><br />There are a lot of themes and ideas explored in this book. Technologies and networks versus nature and ecosystems. Math versus art. Whether the soldiers on opposite sides of a war have more in common with each other than their leaders. It is a very imaginative story. But what makes this book a must-read is the writing generally, and the writing about love specifically. Reread those quotes above again; this novel is literally poetic.<br /><br />I was completely blown away by <i>This is How You Lose the Time War</i>, and am already looking forward to rereading it. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6458923021709231367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2900853863" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2900853863" />
    <a title="Spencer Orey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4227558-spencer-orey"><img alt="Spencer Orey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530700263p2/4227558.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2900853863?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Spencer Orey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Spencer Orey" href="/user/show/4227558-spencer-orey">Spencer Orey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2900853863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11806497226842903939">Really dense time-travel love story novella packed with wonderful writing that focuses on sensory experiences.<br/><br/>There were parts that felt like filler, included in the book more for the beauty of language than anything to do with the plot or story. The episodic structure also made it hard for me to keep focused, since the real story seemed to be unfolding in the letters that punctuated each episode. All of that meant I tended to pick up and put down the book a lot more than I would have otherwise.</span>
  <span id="freeText11806497226842903939" style="display:none">Really dense time-travel love story novella packed with wonderful writing that focuses on sensory experiences.<br /><br />There were parts that felt like filler, included in the book more for the beauty of language than anything to do with the plot or story. The episodic structure also made it hard for me to keep focused, since the real story seemed to be unfolding in the letters that punctuated each episode. All of that meant I tended to pick up and put down the book a lot more than I would have otherwise. <br /><br />But it was thoughtful and cool, and the clashing civilizations were different in really interesting ways.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2878628229?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte">Charlotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11475773-charlotte?shelf=2020-newish">2020-newish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11475773-charlotte?shelf=women-and-nb-of-speculative-fiction">women-and-nb-of-speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11475773-charlotte?shelf=poc-author">poc-author</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2878628229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14873020930068392970"><i>"I want to chase you, find you, I want to be eluded and teased and adored; I want to be defeated and victorious—I want you to cut me, sharpen me."</i><br/><br/>Hello and welcome to my review of 2019's novella <i>This is How you Lose the Time War</i> by Amal El-Mohtar and Max Gladstone. Also known as the review where my bad opinions are made manifest because apparently everyone loved this book except for me!<br/><br/><b>So What's It About? (from Goodreads)</b><br/><br/><i>Among the ashes of a dying world, an agent of the Commandant finds a letter</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14873020930068392970" style="display:none"><i>"I want to chase you, find you, I want to be eluded and teased and adored; I want to be defeated and victorious—I want you to cut me, sharpen me."</i><br /><br />Hello and welcome to my review of 2019's novella <i>This is How you Lose the Time War</i> by Amal El-Mohtar and Max Gladstone. Also known as the review where my bad opinions are made manifest because apparently everyone loved this book except for me!<br /><br /><b>So What's It About? (from Goodreads)</b><br /><br /><i>Among the ashes of a dying world, an agent of the Commandant finds a letter. It reads: Burn before reading.<br /><br />Thus begins an unlikely correspondence between two rival agents hellbent on securing the best possible future for their warring factions. Now, what began as a taunt, a battlefield boast, grows into something more. Something epic. Something romantic. Something that could change the past and the future.<br /><br />Except the discovery of their bond would mean death for each of them. There’s still a war going on, after all. And someone has to win that war. That’s how war works. Right?</i><br /><br /><b>What I Thought</b><br /><br />A enemies-to-lovers f/f romance between time-traveling assassins is just about the coolest premise for a novella that I can think of. I was 100% ready to be blown away! Instead I left this book mostly irritated, and I've been thinking a lot about why since then.<br /><br />Maybe this is a piping hot take, but I honestly struggled to tell a difference between Red and Blue whatsoever. They were both just ruthless, clever agents who sure loved their similes and metaphors.  When I mentioned this on Goodreads I was met with mixed emotions, so I don't know if this is a legitimate concern for most readers. It certainly was for me, though. Someone mentioned that they could tell a difference in the way that they delivered their letters, but to me there was no especially visible pattern, and I'd argue that most of their stories are conveyed in letters that are nearly identical in their writing style and expression.<br /><br />That brings me to the other thing...I really struggled with the prose in this one. And it's not that I'm in any way opposed to convoluted, flowery, elaborate language. You're looking at the girl who spent most of her high school years reading nothing but Victorian lit, after all! When I think about whether elaborate prose feels effective to me or not, it's really just a gut reaction. I don't know why I love authors like Patricia McKillip, Sofia Samatar and Catherynne Valente while this book left me annoyed and rolling my eyes, but that is indeed the state of affairs I arrived at while reading <i>This is How You Lose the Time War.</i> It's just so apparent that it's trying so desperately hard to be poetic and brilliant!<br /><br />I did truly enjoy the structure, and the lovely, vivid imagery of each of the different worlds and moments in history that the agents visited. They see a staggering number of fascinating places and strange moments in history, and I genuinely looked forward to finishing each letter and finding out where Red and Blue were going to be next. The ending was excellent as well - every piece of the story came together in a wholly satisfying and brilliant conclusion that used its time travel mechanics in the best of ways.<br /><br /><b>The F Word</b><br /><br />Well, it's about lesbian android assassins coming to love each other and fight against the systems that entrap them, so uhhhh yeah, I'd say we're doing okay in the feminist department. If you're looking for a novella that is entirely dedicated to a full-hearted queer love story featuring badasses this is definitely a great option, provided you aren't turned off by the things I was turned off by.<br /><br /><b>About the Authors</b><br /><br /><b>Amal El-Mohtar (from her website)</b><br /><br />Amal El-Mohtar is an award-winning writer of fiction, poetry, and criticism. Her stories and poems have appeared in magazines including Tor.com, Fireside Fiction, Lightspeed, Uncanny, Strange Horizons, Apex, Stone Telling, and Mythic Delirium; anthologies including The Djinn Falls in Love and Other Stories (2017), The Starlit Wood: New Fairy Tales (2016), Kaleidoscope: Diverse YA Science Fiction and Fantasy Stories (2014), and The Thackery T. Lambshead Cabinet of Curiosities (2011); and in her own collection, The Honey Month (2010). Her articles and reviews have appeared in the New York Times, NPR Books and on Tor.com. She became the Otherworldly columnist at the New York Times in February 2018, and is represented by DongWon Song of HMLA.<br /><br />Amal has written stories about maps, bird women, book women, the Arabic alphabet, singing fish, Damascene dream-crafters, sentient diamond oceans and pockets that are bigger on the inside. Her story “Seasons of Glass and Iron” won the Nebula, Locus and Hugo awards in 2017, while her stories “The Green Book” and “Madeleine” were finalists for the Nebula Award in 2011 and 2015 respectively, and “The Truth About Owls” won the Locus Award in 2015.<br /><br />Her poems “Song for an Ancient City,” “Peach-Creamed Honey,” and “Turning the Leaves” won the Rhysling award for Best Short Poem in 2009, 2011 and 2014 respectively, and in 2012 she received the Richard Jefferies Poetry Prize for “Phase Shifting.” In her (few) hours of rest she drinks tea, lifts weights, plays harp, and writes letters to her friends by hand.<br /><br /><b>Max Gladstone (from his website)</b><br /><br />Max Gladstone has been thrown from a horse in Mongolia and nominated for the Hugo, John W Campbell, and Lambda Awards. Max’s most recent novels are the intergalactic adventure EMPRESS OF FOREVER, and, with Amal El-Mohtar, the time travel epistolary spy-vs-spy novella THIS IS HOW YOU LOSE THE TIME WAR. Max is also the author of the Hugo-nominated Craft Sequence, starting with THREE PARTS DEAD and most recently continuing in RUIN OF ANGELS, as well as the lead writer for the fantasy procedural series Bookburners.<br /><br />Max regularly consults as a narrative and game designer and world builder, and has written games, comics, and interactive television. His nonfiction appears on Tor.com. Max studied Chan poetry and late Ming dynasty fiction at Yale, and lived and taught for two years in rural Anhui province.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14873020930068392970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name

      }

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/58237743-this-is-how-you-lose-the-time-war">Quotes from This Is How You L...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Books are letters in bottles, cast into the waves of time, from one person trying to save the world to another.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/9893224-books-are-letters-in-bottles-cast-into-the-waves-of">121 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I want to be a body for you. I want to chase you, find you, I want to be eluded and teased and adored; I want to be defeated and victorious—I want you to cut me, sharpen me. I want to drink tea beside you in ten years or a thousand. Flowers grow far away on a planet they’ll call Cephalus, and these flowers bloom once a century, when the living star and its black-hole binary enter conjunction.I want to fix you a bouquet of them, gathered across eight hundred thousand years, so you can draw our whole engagement in a single breath, all the ages we’ve shaped together.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>

This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
React component will render its content.
-->
